data-file-height="290" /></span></span></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section needs to be <b>updated</b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help update this article to reflect recent events or newly available information.</span>  <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">May 2024</span>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_nanotechnology_applications" class="mw-redirect" title="List of nanotechnology applications">List of nanotechnology applications</a></div>
<p>As of August 21, 2008, the <a href="/wiki/Project_on_Emerging_Nanotechnologies" title="Project on Emerging Nanotechnologies">Project on Emerging Nanotechnologies</a> estimated that over 800 manufacturer-identified nanotech products were publicly available, with new ones hitting the market at a pace of 3–4 per week.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-emergingnano&#95;19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-emergingnano-19"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>19<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Most applications are "first generation" passive nanomaterials that includes titanium dioxide in sunscreen, cosmetics, surface coatings,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>60<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and some food products; Carbon allotropes used to produce <a href="/wiki/Gecko_tape" class="mw-redirect" title="Gecko tape">gecko tape</a>; silver in <a href="/wiki/Food_packaging" title="Food packaging">food packaging</a>, clothing, disinfectants, and household appliances; zinc oxide in sunscreens and cosmetics, surface coatings, paints and outdoor furniture varnishes; and cerium oxide as a fuel catalyst.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-americanelements&#95;18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-americanelements-18"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>18<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In the electric car industry, single wall carbon nanotubes (SWCNTs) address key <a href="/wiki/Lithium-ion_battery" title="Lithium-ion battery">lithium-ion battery</a> challenges, including energy density, charge rate, service life, and cost. SWCNTs connect electrode particles during charge/discharge process, preventing battery premature degradation. Their exceptional ability to wrap active material particles enhanced electrical conductivity and physical properties, setting them apart multi-walled carbon nanotubes and carbon black.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>61<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>62<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>63<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Further applications allow <a href="/wiki/Tennis_ball" title="Tennis ball">tennis balls</a> to last longer, <a href="/wiki/Golf_ball" title="Golf ball">golf balls</a> to fly straighter, and <a href="/wiki/Bowling_ball" title="Bowling ball">bowling balls</a> to become more durable. <a href="/wiki/Trouser" class="mw-redirect" title="Trouser">Trousers</a> and <a href="/wiki/Socks" class="mw-redirect" title="Socks">socks</a> have been infused with nanotechnology to last longer and lower temperature in the summer. <a href="/wiki/Bandage" title="Bandage">Bandages</a> are infused with silver nanoparticles to heal cuts faster.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-nnin&#95;64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nnin-64"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>64<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Video_game_console" title="Video game console">Video game consoles</a> and <a href="/wiki/Personal_computer" title="Personal computer">personal computers</a> may become cheaper, faster, and contain more memory thanks to nanotechnology.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>65<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Also, to build structures for on chip computing with light, for example on chip optical quantum information processing, and picosecond transmission of information.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>66<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Nanotechnology may have the ability to make existing medical applications cheaper and easier to use in places like the doctors' offices and at homes.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>67<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Cars use <a href="/wiki/Nanomaterial" class="mw-redirect" title="Nanomaterial">nanomaterials</a> in such ways that car parts require fewer <a href="/wiki/Metal" title="Metal">metals</a> during manufacturing and less <a href="/wiki/Fuel" title="Fuel">fuel</a> to operate in the future.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>68<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Nanoencapsulation involves the enclosure of active substances within carriers. Typically, these carriers offer advantages, such as enhanced bioavailability, controlled release, targeted delivery, and protection of the encapsulated substances. In the medical field, nanoencapsulation plays a significant role in <a href="/wiki/Drug_delivery" title="Drug delivery">drug delivery</a>. It facilitates more efficient drug administration, reduces side effects, and increases treatment effectiveness. Nanoencapsulation is particularly useful for improving the bioavailability of poorly water-soluble drugs, enabling controlled and sustained drug release, and supporting the development of targeted therapies. These features collectively contribute to advancements in medical treatments and patient care.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>69<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>70<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Nanotechnology may play role in <a href="/wiki/Tissue_Engineering" class="mw-redirect" title="Tissue Engineering">tissue engineering</a>. When designing scaffolds, researchers attempt to mimic the nanoscale features of a <a href="/wiki/Cell_(biology)" title="Cell (biology)">cell</a>'s microenvironment to direct its differentiation down a suitable lineage.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>71<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> For example, when creating scaffolds to support bone growth, researchers may mimic <a href="/wiki/Osteoclast" title="Osteoclast">osteoclast</a> resorption pits.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>72<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Researchers used <a href="/wiki/DNA_origami" title="DNA origami">DNA origami</a>-based nanobots capable of carrying out logic functions to target drug delivery in cockroaches.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>73<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>A nano bible (a .5mm2 silicon chip) was created by the <a href="/wiki/Technion_%E2%80%93_Israel_Institute_of_Technology" title="Technion – Israel Institute of Technology">Technion</a> in order to increase youth interest in nanotechnology.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>74<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Implications">Implications</h2></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Implications_of_nanotechnology" class="mw-redirect" title="Implications of nanotechnology">Implications of nanotechnology</a></div>
<p>One concern is the effect that industrial-scale manufacturing and use of nanomaterials will have on human health and the environment, as suggested by <a href="/wiki/Nanotoxicology" title="Nanotoxicology">nanotoxicology</a> research. For these reasons, some groups advocate that nanotechnology be regulated. However, regulation might stifle scientific research and the development of beneficial innovations. <a href="/wiki/Public_health" title="Public health">Public health</a> research agencies, such as the <a href="/wiki/National_Institute_for_Occupational_Safety_and_Health" title="National Institute for Occupational Safety and Health">National Institute for Occupational Safety and Health</a> research potential health effects stemming from exposures to nanoparticles.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-niosh&#95;75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-niosh-75"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>75<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-nioshnano&#95;76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nioshnano-76"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>76<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Nanoparticle products may have <a href="/wiki/Unintended_consequences" title="Unintended consequences">unintended consequences</a>. Researchers have discovered that <a href="/wiki/Bacteriostatic" class="mw-redirect" title="Bacteriostatic">bacteriostatic</a> silver nanoparticles used in socks to reduce foot odor are released in the wash.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>77<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> These particles are then flushed into the wastewater stream and may destroy bacteria that are critical components of natural ecosystems, farms, and waste treatment processes.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>78<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Public deliberations on <a href="/wiki/Risk_perception" title="Risk perception">risk perception</a> in the US and UK carried out by the Center for Nanotechnology in Society found that participants were more positive about nanotechnologies for energy applications than for health applications, with health applications raising moral and ethical dilemmas such as cost and availability.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-harthorn&#95;79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-harthorn-79"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>79<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Experts, including director of the Woodrow Wilson Center's Project on Emerging Nanotechnologies David Rejeski, testified<sup id="cite&#95;ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>80<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> that commercialization depends on adequate oversight, risk research strategy, and public engagement. As of 206 <a href="/wiki/Berkeley,_California" title="Berkeley, California">Berkeley, California</a> was the only US city to regulate nanotechnology.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>81<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Health_and_environmental_concerns">Health and environmental concerns</h3></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><span><video id="mwe_player_1" poster="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/NIOSH_Nano_Research_-_Engineering_Controls_for_Nanomaterial_Production_and_Handling_Processes.webm/250px--NIOSH_Nano_Research_-_Engineering_Controls_for_Nanomaterial_Production_and_Handling_Processes.webm.jpg" controls="" preload="none" data-mw-tmh="" class="mw-file-element" width="250" height="141" data-durationhint="270" data-mwtitle="NIOSH_Nano_Research_-_Engineering_Controls_for_Nanomaterial_Production_and_Handling_Processes.webm" data-mwprovider="wikimediacommons" resource="/wiki/File:NIOSH_Nano_Research_-_Engineering_Controls_for_Nanomaterial_Production_and_Handling_Processes.webm"><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/2/21/NIOSH_Nano_Research_-_Engineering_Controls_for_Nanomaterial_Production_and_Handling_Processes.webm/NIOSH_Nano_Research_-_Engineering_Controls_for_Nanomaterial_Production_and_Handling_Processes.webm.480p.vp9.webm" type="video/webm; codecs=&quot;vp9, opus&quot;" data-transcodekey="480p.vp9.webm" data-width="854" data-height="480" /><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/2/21/NIOSH_Nano_Research_-_Engineering_Controls_for_Nanomaterial_Production_and_Handling_Processes.webm/NIOSH_Nano_Research_-_Engineering_Controls_for_Nanomaterial_Production_and_Handling_Processes.webm.1080p.vp9.webm" type="video/webm; codecs=&quot;vp9, opus&quot;" data-transcodekey="1080p.vp9.webm" data-width="1920" data-height="1080" /><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/21/NIOSH_Nano_Research_-_Engineering_Controls_for_Nanomaterial_Production_and_Handling_Processes.webm" type="video/webm; codecs=&quot;vp8, vorbis&quot;" data-width="1920" data-height="1080" /><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/2/21/NIOSH_Nano_Research_-_Engineering_Controls_for_Nanomaterial_Production_and_Handling_Processes.webm/NIOSH_Nano_Research_-_Engineering_Controls_for_Nanomaterial_Production_and_Handling_Processes.webm.144p.mjpeg.mov" type="video/quicktime" data-transcodekey="144p.mjpeg.mov" data-width="256" data-height="144" /><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/2/21/NIOSH_Nano_Research_-_Engineering_Controls_for_Nanomaterial_Production_and_Handling_Processes.webm/NIOSH_Nano_Research_-_Engineering_Controls_for_Nanomaterial_Production_and_Handling_Processes.webm.240p.vp9.webm" type="video/webm; codecs=&quot;vp9, opus&quot;" data-transcodekey="240p.vp9.webm" data-width="426" data-height="240" /><track src="https://commons.wikimedia.org/w/api.php?action=timedtext&amp;title=File%3ANIOSH_Nano_Research_-_Engineering_Controls_for_Nanomaterial_Production_and_Handling_Processes.webm&amp;lang=en&amp;trackformat=vtt&amp;origin=%2A" kind="subtitles" type="text/vtt" srclang="en" label="English ‪(en)‬" data-dir="ltr" /></video></span><figcaption>A video on the health and safety implications of nanotechnology</figcaption></figure>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Health_and_safety_hazards_of_nanomaterials" title="Health and safety hazards of nanomaterials">Health and safety hazards of nanomaterials</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pollution_from_nanomaterials" title="Pollution from nanomaterials">Pollution from nanomaterials</a></div>
<p>Inhaling airborne nanoparticles and nanofibers may contribute to <a href="/wiki/Pulmonary_disease" class="mw-redirect" title="Pulmonary disease">pulmonary diseases</a>, e.g. <a href="/wiki/Fibrosis" title="Fibrosis">fibrosis</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>82<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Researchers found that when rats breathed in nanoparticles, the particles settled in the brain and lungs, which led to significant increases in biomarkers for inflammation and stress response<sup id="cite&#95;ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>83<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and that nanoparticles induce skin aging through <a href="/wiki/Oxidative_stress" title="Oxidative stress">oxidative stress</a> in hairless mice.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>84<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>85<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>A two-year study at <a href="/wiki/UCLA_Fielding_School_of_Public_Health" title="UCLA Fielding School of Public Health">UCLA's School of Public Health</a> found lab mice consuming nano-titanium dioxide showed DNA and chromosome damage to a degree "linked to all the big killers of man, namely cancer, heart disease, neurological disease and aging".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>86<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>A <i><a href="/wiki/Nature_Nanotechnology" title="Nature Nanotechnology">Nature Nanotechnology</a></i> study suggested that some forms of <a href="/wiki/Carbon_nanotube" title="Carbon nanotube">carbon nanotubes</a> could be as harmful as <a href="/wiki/Asbestos" title="Asbestos">asbestos</a> if inhaled in sufficient quantities. <a href="/wiki/Anthony_Seaton" title="Anthony Seaton">Anthony Seaton</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Institute_of_Occupational_Medicine" title="Institute of Occupational Medicine">Institute of Occupational Medicine</a> in Edinburgh, Scotland, who contributed to the article on <a href="/wiki/Carbon_nanotube" title="Carbon nanotube">carbon nanotubes</a> said "We know that some of them probably have the potential to cause <a href="/wiki/Mesothelioma" title="Mesothelioma">mesothelioma</a>. So those sorts of materials need to be handled very carefully."<sup id="cite&#95;ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>87<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In the absence of specific regulation forthcoming from governments, Paull and Lyons (2008) have called for an exclusion of engineered nanoparticles in food.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>88<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> A newspaper article reports that workers in a paint factory developed serious lung disease and nanoparticles were found in their lungs.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>89<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>90<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>91<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>92<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Regulation">Regulation</h2></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Regulation_of_nanotechnology" title="Regulation of nanotechnology">Regulation of nanotechnology</a></div>
<p>Calls for tighter regulation of nanotechnology have accompanied a debate related to human health and safety risks.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>93<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Some regulatory agencies cover some nanotechnology products and processes – by "bolting on" nanotechnology to existing regulations – leaving clear gaps.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>94<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Davies proposed a road map describing steps to deal with these shortcomings.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>95<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Andrew Maynard, chief science advisor to the Woodrow Wilson Center's Project on Emerging Nanotechnologies, reported insufficient funding for human health and safety research, and as a result inadequate understanding of human health and safety risks.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>96<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Some academics called for stricter application of the <a href="/wiki/Precautionary_principle" title="Precautionary principle">precautionary principle</a>, slowing marketing approval, enhanced labelling and additional safety data.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>97<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>A Royal Society report identified a risk of nanoparticles or nanotubes being released during disposal, destruction and recycling, and recommended that "manufacturers of products that fall under <a href="/wiki/Extended_producer_responsibility" title="Extended producer responsibility">extended producer responsibility</a> regimes such as end-of-life regulations publish procedures outlining how these materials will be managed to minimize possible human and environmental exposure".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-royalsociety&#95;16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-royalsociety-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
